# Platform Build Log

Append-only log of work sessions. Each session adds exactly one row, in two edits:

1. **At session start** (before any real work): append a row with status `⏳ IN FLIGHT — {step name}`, commit it immediately as its own standalone commit.
2. **At session end** (after the real work is done, tested, and typechecked): update that same row to `✅ DONE — {step name}`, filling in the real commit hash of the work, then commit the update (either folded into the final commit or immediately after it).

If a session dies, crashes, or is abandoned mid-way, its row stays `⏳ IN FLIGHT`, which is itself the record that an attempt was made and didn't finish.

See [CLAUDE.md](CLAUDE.md) for the exact instructions.

| Date | Status | Step | Commit |
|------|--------|------|--------|
| 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | License-Gap Classification — Unblock Docs, Honest Copy, Real Upsell — a real cross-cutting fix for tenants missing M365 add-ons (no Entra ID Premium / Defender for Office 365), a common real-customer situation. ROOT CAUSE (traced, not assumed): Graph checks that fail because the tenant lacks a SKU were conflated with two unrelated states. A 401 `Unauthorized — Account is not provisioned` hit `graphFetchForTenant`'s blanket "any 401 → consent revoked" path → `markTenantConsentRevoked()` bulk-flipped EVERY `tenant_monitor_profiles` row for the tenant to `consent_revoked` (a tenant-wide contamination from one unprovisioned feature) + threw `ConsentRevokedError` (which then short-circuited all remaining checks); a 403 `Authentication_RequestFromNonPremiumTenantOrB2CTenant` fell through `isConsentErrorBody` and surfaced as a generic `error`. Either way `pkgResult.runStatus` became `consent_revoked`/`partial_failure`, so `diagnostics-runner`'s `finalStatus` never reached `"completed"` — and the seeded Assessment Document Generation workflow's `assessment_doc_gate` requires `msp_diagnostic_runs.status = 'completed'`, so a license-gapped tenant could NEVER get documents generated. FIX (D1) `graph.ts`: new `classifyGraphError()` + `LicenseGapError`; `graphFetchForTenant` now reads the 401/400/403 body and, on a documented AAD premium error CODE (`Authentication_RequestFromNonPremiumTenantOrB2CTenant`/`RequestFromNonPremiumTenantOrB2CTenant`) or the stable `"not provisioned"` / `"doesn't have premium license"` phrases, throws `LicenseGapError` with a customer-safe feature name and does NOT flip consent — genuine consent errors (`invalid_grant`/`AADSTS65001`/`consent_required`/`InvalidAuthenticationToken`, and any other bare 401) still auto-revoke exactly as before; only these exact structural signals are reclassified (no fragile heuristic, per the no-silent-reclassification rule). (D2) `monitor-executor.ts`: new `"license_gap"` `CheckResult` status — license gaps no longer set the consent short-circuit (each check may need a different SKU, so all checks now run), and the run-status computation treats them as neither error nor consent_revoked, so a tenant whose only non-ok results are license gaps reaches `"completed"` HONESTLY, unblocking the doc gate WITHOUT weakening the gate's own `= 'completed'` check (fixed upstream, per non-goal). Adds `licenseGapCount`/`licenseGapFeatures` to `PackageRunResult` + `licenseGap` to the engine breakdown, and stamps definitive falsy license flags (`hasAADP1orP2:false`/`hasDefender:false` — the same keys the M365 script parser writes) into the license_gap profile row so the existing signal engine can derive an upsell signal off a Graph-only scan. `diagnostics-runner.ts`: license_gap findings are `info` (never critical/red), counted in the new `checks_license_gap` column + run `summary.licenseGapFeatures`, named in the HTML report's summary; `finalStatus` now reaches `completed` via the upstream fix (unchanged mapping). (D3) `portal-assessment.ts` exposes `checksLicenseGap` + `licenseGapFeatures` from the run/summary; `AssessmentWizard.tsx` scan-complete copy now reads e.g. "9 checks passed. Now writing up your findings… N checks couldn't run because your tenant doesn't have Microsoft Entra ID Premium (P1/P2) or Microsoft Defender for Office 365 — that's a licensing gap, not a security issue." and scores the ring over EVALUABLE checks (ok+error, excluding license gaps) so a fully-passing-but-unlicensed tenant reads green, not "31% red". Reuses the backend classification — no second frontend derivation. (D4 — investigate-and-wire-if-clean) Confirmed via subagent trace: the Sales Offer Engine is signal-driven off `client_m365_profiles`/`tenant_monitor_profiles` (NOT diagnostic findings), and there IS a clean INPUT seam (this work now writes `hasAADP1orP2/hasDefender:false` + a `license_upsell` recommendation with `signalKey` = `security:lacks_entra_premium`/`security:lacks_defender`). But the OUTPUT side (`sales_offer_rule_groups`) has NO seed and needs admin-configured catalog products + pricing (no-hardcoding rule), so wiring an end-to-end offer would be a parallel, un-seeded mechanism — reported as a FOLLOW-UP (add `custom_signals` rows + `signal_derivation_rules` of type `profile_key_falsy` on those keys + catalog services + eligibility rule groups) rather than built, per the non-goal. (D5) No live DB/tenant in this env: verified by clean `tsc --noEmit` on api-server + msp-portal, and unit tests proving the full chain — `LicenseGapError` on a premium 403 and a not-provisioned 401 with NO consent flip (no transaction/audit), `classifyGraphError` classification table, run reaches `completed` with license gaps + no short-circuit + both checks actually run, and the falsy license flags are stamped; traced the `completed` status → `assessment_doc_gate`'s `eq(status,'completed')` match → generation proceeds. Also repaired a pre-existing `logger.child`-missing mock gap in the two affected test files (both were failing at HEAD since graph.ts/monitor-executor call `logger.child` at module load) and a latent fetch-mock once-queue leak. Manual SQL shipped: `2026-07-21-diagnostic-runs-license-gap.sql` (one `ALTER TABLE msp_diagnostic_runs ADD COLUMN checks_license_gap`; the `license_gap` status needs no DDL — plain text column). Committed pathspec-scoped to my 9 files; concurrent-session work on `AssessmentWizard.tsx` was already in HEAD and left untouched. | 512cf684 |

| 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Fix Bulk Consent-Revoke Overwrite Stomping on Correctly-Classified license_gap Rows — confirmed live regression in the already-landed License-Gap Classification work (512cf684): `markTenantConsentRevoked()` in `graph.ts` bulk-updates every `tenant_monitor_profiles` row for a tenant to `status: "consent_revoked"` whenever any check in a run genuinely throws `ConsentRevokedError`, with no exclusion for rows already correctly classified `"license_gap"` by the separate `LicenseGapError` path in `monitor-executor.ts` — the WHERE clause only excluded rows already `consent_revoked`. Traced the real mechanism: `executeMonitorCheck`'s idempotency guard replays a cached DB row keyed on `(tenantId, checkKey, triggerId)`, so once a license_gap row is stomped, a same-`triggerId` retry of that run permanently replays the wrong classification, blocking `diagnostics-runner`'s `finalStatus` from ever reaching `"completed"` for a tenant whose only non-ok results are genuine license gaps — directly undermining the intended outcome of 512cf684. FIX: added `ne(tenantMonitorProfilesTable.status, "license_gap")` alongside the existing `ne(..., "consent_revoked")` exclusion in the bulk update's WHERE clause (`graph.ts`), preserving the bulk-revoke's legitimate purpose for genuinely-affected rows. Did not touch `classifyGraphError`/`LicenseGapError` classification (confirmed already correct, per non-goal) or the run-status computation in `monitor-executor.ts`/`diagnostics-runner.ts` (confirmed already correctly excludes license_gap from failure counts, per non-goal) — this is purely a downstream-overwrite fix. VERIFIED: added a new unit test to `graph-consent-revoke.test.ts` asserting the bulk update's WHERE clause structurally contains `ne(status, "license_gap")` (drizzle-orm mocked as structural objects so the actual condition shape is inspectable, not just the `set()` payload) — all 75 tests in the two affected suites (`graph-consent-revoke.test.ts`, `monitor-executor.test.ts`) pass; clean `tsc -p tsconfig.json --noEmit` in `artifacts/api-server`. | 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Fix Typewriter Headline Randomization + Repeat Bug — confirmed root cause of both bugs by tracing `useHeroHeadlines.ts` + the seed SQL: `FALLBACK_HEADLINE`'s text is byte-identical to the DB's `sort_order = 0` row (`2026-07-19-hero-headlines.sql`), and the hook seeded `headlines` state to `[FALLBACK_HEADLINE]` (array length 1) before the `/api/public/hero-headlines` fetch resolved. Since `headlineIndex % headlines.length` is always `0 % 1 = 0`, the rotation was trapped on that single entry — typing, pausing, and deleting it in a full loop, potentially more than once — for however long the fetch took; because that entry's text is identical to the real first headline, this was visually indistinguishable from "the first headline plays twice" before the real rotation ever started. Separately, `public-hero.ts` always returned rows `orderBy(asc(sortOrder))` and nothing on the client ever reordered them, so rotation order was always fixed DB order. FIX: added a `loaded` flag set once the fetch settles (success, empty, or failure); while unloaded and still on the 1-element fallback array, the typing effect now holds at the fully-typed fallback instead of deleting/retyping it in a loop. On successful fetch, the headline set is now shuffled once (Fisher-Yates) before being stored, and `headlineIndex`/`charCount`/`phase` are reset so the real rotation starts clean at a random order — not re-shuffled on every cycle, only once per page load. Only `useHeroHeadlines.ts` touched — `Home.tsx`, the admin Hero Headlines management screen, and headline content untouched, per task scope. `shane-mccaw-consulting` typechecks clean (`npx tsc -p tsconfig.json --noEmit`, exit 0). Not clicked through in a live browser in this environment (no dev server running this session) — verified by full code trace of the fetch → state → effect chain plus the confirmed seed-data match, and clean typecheck. | 2621845e |

| 2026-07-20 | ✅ DONE | Defender for Endpoint App-Only Write Integration — connection/auth layer only (no `baseline_action_templates` wiring, same as the parallel SharePoint task). New `lib/defender-endpoint.ts` is a THIRD Microsoft resource audience layered on the SAME multi-tenant App Registration graph.ts already drives — NOT Microsoft Graph. Read graph.ts in full first and replicated its patterns exactly rather than inventing a parallel mechanism: token acquisition modeled on `getAccessTokenForTenant`/`getActivityApiToken` (v2.0 `client_credentials` `.default` flow reusing the SAME `MT_APP_CLIENT_ID`/`MT_APP_CLIENT_SECRET` env credentials — confirmed via code read those are the shared client-secret creds, no certificate and no duplicate secret storage), a per-tenant `Map<string,TokenCache>` identical in shape to graph.ts's `tenantTokenCache`/`activityTokenCache`, and the `graphWriteForTenant` typed-result convention. AUDIT-FIRST findings, all verified directly against current Microsoft Learn API reference (2025-11/2026-02 revisions), not guessed: (1) isolate = `POST https://api.security.microsoft.com/api/machines/{id}/isolate`, body `{ Comment (required), IsolationType: "Full"|"Selective"|"UnManagedDevice" }`, Application permission `Machine.Isolate`; (2) release-from-isolation = `POST .../unisolate`, body `{ Comment }`, same `Machine.Isolate` permission; (3) run-AV-scan = `POST .../runAntiVirusScan`, body `{ Comment (required), ScanType: "Quick"|"Full" }`, Application permission `Machine.Scan` (confirmed the real permission name — NOT a guessed "Machine.RunAntivirus"). All three return 201 Created + a MachineAction resource (typed). These permissions are granted under the **WindowsDefenderATP** API surface in the app registration, SEPARATE from Microsoft Graph — so documented them in a new exported `REQUIRED_DEFENDER_APP_PERMISSIONS` const in this file, deliberately NOT added to graph.ts's `REQUIRED_MT_SCOPES` (that is the Graph `.default` consent set; mixing a non-Graph scope in would break Graph token acquisition), with a comment that adding them forces fresh admin re-consent on every tenant. CRITICAL TOKEN-AUDIENCE GOTCHA baked in with a citing comment (Microsoft's own docs): the token scope is the LEGACY resource `https://api.securitycenter.microsoft.com/.default` even though the request host is `api.security.microsoft.com` — a mismatched audience returns 403 even against the right endpoint; do not "fix" the mismatch. Regional host variants (`us.`/`eu.`) overridable via `DEFENDER_ENDPOINT_API_BASE` env without a code change. DELIBERATE DESIGN DECISION (operational-risk-driven): Defender consent errors throw a dedicated `DefenderConsentError` and do NOT call graph.ts's `markTenantConsentRevoked` — Defender permission consent is a SEPARATE consent surface from the shared Graph `tenant_consent` row, and a tenant with valid Graph consent but no Defender re-consent returns AADSTS65001; flipping the Graph consent row there would wrongly disable working Graph monitoring (the exact collateral damage this integration must avoid). This layer evicts only its own token cache. All three write functions require a non-empty operator `Comment` (Microsoft requires it + it is Defender's audit trail); 403-insufficient-privilege / 409-conflict / "already in progress" / 404 surfaced as typed non-throwing results, only re-consent and network errors propagate. `integration.defender` added as a new leaf channel under the existing `integration.*` taxonomy (task-sanctioned). Documented 100 calls/min + 1,500/hr rate limits in a comment; no rate-limiting infra built (out of scope) — just a "don't call in a tight loop" note. api-server typechecks clean (only the pre-existing `health-engine.test.ts` TS2698 debt remains, consistent with prior sessions; zero Defender-related errors). Not live-tested against a real Defender tenant (no DB/live Graph/Defender access in this environment) — verified by full code trace + direct doc confirmation of every endpoint/body/permission/audience. No schema/migration changes (no `drizzle-kit push`). | a3224ce4 |

AUDIT (documented in `sharepoint-admin.README.md`, confirmed via Microsoft Learn, not guessed): (1) required Application permission is `Sites.FullControl.All` under the **Office 365 SharePoint Online** resource (`00000003-0000-0ff1-ce00-000000000000`) — NOT Graph, same way `Exchange.ManageAsApp` sits under Office 365 Exchange Online; narrower `Sites.Manage.All`/`Sites.Selected` are insufficient for tenant admin. Also exported in code as `REQUIRED_SHAREPOINT_APP_PERMISSIONS` (mirrors `graph.ts`'s `REQUIRED_MT_SCOPES`, kept separate as that array is Graph `.default` only). (2) CRITICAL AUTH FINDING surfaced not papered over: SharePoint **rejects client-secret app-only tokens** ("unsupported app only token"/401) and mandates a **certificate** (`client_assertion` JWT). The MT app today has only `MT_APP_CLIENT_SECRET` — so this module uses RS256 cert client-assertion (same `jsonwebtoken` idiom as `search-console.ts`, x5t = base64url of the SHA-1 thumbprint) reading two NEW env vars `MT_APP_CERT_PRIVATE_KEY` + `MT_APP_CERT_THUMBPRINT`; `sharePointAdminCredentialsPresent()` guards on them and deliberately does NOT accept the secret. Flagged as an open platform-owner item: a cert must be added to the existing MT app registration (or the Exchange app-only cert reused) + `Sites.FullControl.All` granted/consented before these functions authenticate. (3) Endpoint shapes confirmed per Microsoft docs, not assumed from PnP cmdlet names: `createSiteCollection`/`deleteSiteCollection`/`getSiteStatus` use documented SPSiteManager JSON REST (`POST /_api/SPSiteManager/create` — `Owner` REQUIRED in app-only — `/delete` `{siteId}`, `GET /status`); `get/setTenantSharingCapability` + `get/setSiteStorageQuota` have NO documented REST equivalent (the exact trap the task warned of — `Set-SPOTenant`/`Set-SPOSite` don't map to a REST path) so use CSOM `ProcessQuery` XML posted via `fetch` (a direct REST call, NOT PowerShell/PnP invocation) against the admin host, with well-known Tenant `TypeId` `{268004ae-…}`; those CSOM ObjectPath payloads are reverse-engineered/index-sensitive and README-flagged as needing live-tenant validation before the later `baseline_action_templates` wiring. `SharePointAuthError` on 401 evicts only the SP token cache and does NOT flip the shared `tenant_consent`/monitor rows (a SP 401 is ambiguous — missing cert / ungranted permission — not necessarily Graph consent revocation). | 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Fix Direct-Business Customer Login — confirmed via live testing (Shane's own account, a direct-business customer) that `/login`'s real gate mechanism (`POST /api/public/checkout/gate`, `msp-onboarding.ts`) returned `action:"proceed"` with no `portalUrl` for direct-business customers, dead-ending at Login.tsx's "we couldn't find an active portal account" message with no real way to log in. ROOT CAUSE (pure query-logic gap, not structural — confirmed via full code read before touching anything): the gate handler queried `msp_users`/`msps` for an active membership row, correctly found one, then hit `if (!mspUser || mspUser.isDirectBusiness) { return proceed }` — an explicit, deliberate exclusion that discarded a real, found membership row solely because its MSP happened to be the platform's own direct-business MSP (`msps.is_direct_business = true`). The redirect-building code two lines below that check (`mspUser.mspDomain ? https://domain : PORTAL_BASE_URL`) already handles a null custom domain correctly by falling back to the shared `PORTAL_BASE_URL` (the same fallback path any reseller MSP without its own custom domain already uses) — the direct-business MSP has no custom domain of its own, so this fallback is exactly the correct portal URL for it, no new resolution logic needed. FIX: removed the `isDirectBusiness` field from the select + removed `|| mspUser.isDirectBusiness` from the early-return condition (7-line diff, `msp-onboarding.ts`) — a direct-business customer's real membership row now flows through the exact same `action:"redirect"` path a reseller customer's already does. `Login.tsx` confirmed via code read to need zero changes — it already renders generically off `action`/`portalUrl`/`mspName` with no `isDirectBusiness` awareness at all. Updated `msp-onboarding.test.ts`'s two direct-business cases (previously asserting `proceed`) to assert `redirect` with the portal-base-url fallback; all 21 tests in the file pass. `api-server` typechecks clean for both changed files (only pre-existing, already-documented debt remains: `health-engine.test.ts` TS2698, and `document-generator.ts`'s concurrent Database-Driven-Document-Types work — neither touched here). No live DB in this environment (per `CLAUDE.md`) — could not simulate against Shane's actual real account row; correctness verified instead by full code trace of the exact query + resolution path plus the updated unit tests. **CONCURRENCY INCIDENT:** despite staging only this task's own 2 files via explicit pathspec, a fast-moving concurrent session's own broader commit (`dab75cd5`, "Unify Tenant Signal Catalog into custom_signals") landed and swept up the shared git index — including these 2 already-staged files — before this session's own `git commit` could run; by the time this session's commit attempt executed, both files were already part of `dab75cd5` and there was nothing left to commit standalone. The fix itself is correct and fully present in the tree (verified post-hoc via grep + diff re-read) — only the commit boundary is not clean, same class of incident this file's own history already documents repeatedly (see the `8a9b98e7`/`453c4723` rows' own CONCURRENCY NOTEs). | 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE | Fix Stage-Cycle Jump Bug + Lower Score Stage Starting Value — confirmed both issues live before touching code. (1) HowItWorksShowcase.tsx's auto-advance effect had `active` in its own dependency array alongside pausedByPanel/pausedByFocus/inView, so every single auto-advance tick tore down and recreated the interval — racing against those other flags toggling mid-cycle and occasionally landing the loop on the wrong stage instead of a clean 1→2→3→4→5→1 loop. FIX: removed `active` from the effect's deps (the interval's own functional setActive updater already advances correctly without it) and added a `restartToken` state, bumped only by a manual hover/click selection (never by the auto-advance tick itself), so a manual retarget still restarts the countdown from a full stage duration — preserving that intentional feature without the race. (2) solutionsTopics.ts governance topic's dashboard.ringValue (shared by the main "What You Get" score ring and the Score/Remediate stages) was 74, not a compelling "before" state; lowered to 61 (still amber tier per PillarScoreRing's scoreTone: 60-84 amber, <60 red — picked to stay in-tier per task direction rather than drop into red), remediatedRingValue kept at 85 (green-tier floor) for a clear before/after. VERIFIED live via Playwright against the real vite dev server (MSYS_NO_PATHCONV=1 PORT/BASE_PATH, per the admin-panel-local-vite-windows recipe): polled the stage rail's aria-pressed state every second for 46s — two full clean 1→2→3→4→5→1 loops, no jumps; screenshots confirm the Score stage ring, the Remediate before/after rings (61 amber → 85 green), and the page's main "What You Get" ring all read 61 consistently. shane-mccaw-consulting typechecks clean (npx tsc -p tsconfig.json --noEmit, exit 0). CONCURRENCY: a concurrent session was actively finishing the same HowItWorksShowcase.tsx component (its own "Animated 5-Stage How It Works Visual" task, adding crossfade/StageCell, WCAG 2.2.2 persistent pause, etc.) at the same time — both sessions' work landed together in that session's own commit 9c90360c, which explicitly attributes and preserves this task's restartToken fix and the 74→61 lowering (and extends the 61 rescaling into pillarBreakdown/surfaceRadar for scenario coherence, which this task did not touch). | 2026-07-21 | ✅ DONE — Site-Wide Forced-Refresh Bug: Root Cause Investigation — root-caused via live Playwright (not a guess) and DISPROVED the shared/global-component hypothesis: there is NO browser-reload path anywhere in the app (exhaustive grep + full read of every Layout-mounted component — no `location.reload`, no `<meta http-equiv=refresh>`, no service worker, no chunk-error reload handler, no error boundary; the only scroll listeners are BackToTop setting a bool + the analytics tracker firing beacons; recharts, Governance's only lazy import, is pre-bundled at Vite's startup scan so scroll-to-chart never re-optimizes). CONFIRMED ROOT CAUSE: a **Vite dev-server HMR full-page reload**, issued whenever a CONCURRENT editor/session saves a source module in the root import chain (or one whose HMR update can't be accepted and propagates to the entry) — it reloads EVERY open tab at once, independent of page or scroll position. The scroll correlation is coincidental (Governance/Monitoring are long multi-second reads, so a background file-save lands mid-scroll). EVIDENCE (live Playwright, 3 full down+up scroll passes/page): production build (vite build+preview, no HMR) = 0 reloads on both pages fully rendered; isolated single dev server (own cold cacheDir, own port) = 0 reloads on both; shared 5-server dev env = reloads seen but uncorrelated with scroll, with a concurrent session's `[vite] hot updated: Monitoring.tsx`+`index.css` observed live mid-test. DEFINITIVE controlled experiment: two tabs held STILL mid-page, then saving `src/main.tsx` (entry) → FULL RELOAD on BOTH tabs (docLoads 1→2, `[vite] connecting…` reboot) with zero scrolling; saving `analytics.ts`/`button.tsx`/`utils.ts` → app-wide `[vite] invalidate … Could not Fast Refresh` on both idle tabs. Amplifiers (dev-experience only, not user-facing): 5 concurrent dev servers sharing one `node_modules/.vite` cache; Fast-Refresh-incompatible mixed exports in `usePersonalizationState.tsx` (global, consumed by Layout on every page), `button.tsx`/`badge.tsx`/`form.tsx`. NO app code changed — per the task's own "no speculative fix" guardrail and because the reproduced cause is a dev-environment artifact absent from production, there is nothing to fix in runtime code (a save to a genuine root module always full-reloads — correct Vite behavior). Full write-up + reproduction steps in `artifacts/shane-mccaw-consulting/FORCED_REFRESH_INVESTIGATION.md`. Did NOT touch concurrent sessions' dirty files (Home.tsx et al.) or their stray `__*.mjs`/`vite_*.log` probes. | 1bc94616 |
